A list of major specifications, together with their common applications.

PRODUCT         APPLICATION

ASTM 554        Direct Off Mill tube (dom and dom polished) for structural, architectural, automotive
DIN 2463        exhaust, and non-pressure applications.

ASTM A 270      Austenitic bead-rolled tubing for use in the food and beverage industries and austenitic
DIN 1 1850      Sanitary Tube (with special finishes); for use in food, dairy and beverage applications.

ASTM A 789      Tubing for general service.

  ASTM A 269    Austenitic tubing for general service.
DIN 2463/17440

  ASTM A 249    Austenitic tubing for boilers, super heater, heat exchanger and condenser duty.
DIN 2463/17457

  ASTM A 312    Austenitic schedule piping for high temperature and general service.
DIN 2463/17455

ASTM A 688      Austenitic tubing for feedwater heaters and general service.

ASTM A 731      Ferritic and martensitic piping for general service.

ASTM A 790      Ferritic and Austenitic piping for general service.

ASTM A 268      Ferritic and martensitic tubing for general service.

ASTM A 778      Spirally welded austenitic and ferritic tubing for gerneral service.

The South Africa Tube, Pipe and automotive component Manufacturers regularly produce products to these specifications
in a variety of wall thicknesses and diameters.

                                                                                     TABLE
                                            Nominal composition of some of the more common grades of stainless steel
                          Similar grades (on the basis of composition only) from the ASTM & EN Standards are grouped together

NOTES:
1. Nominal compositions are given in this table. These must not be used for specification purposes. For the exact composition reference must be made

   to the appropriate Specification
2. The % content is a maximum unless a compositional range is given
3. Al = aluminium ~ C = carbon ~ Cr = chromium ~ Cu = copper ~ Mn = manganese ~ Mo = molybdenum ~ N = nitrogen ~ Nb = niobium (as Cb =

   columbium in American Specifications) ~ Ni = nickel ~ P = phosphorus ~ S = sulphur ~ Se = selenium ~ Si = silicon ~ Ti = titanium ~ V = vanadium
4. Only the primary alloying elements (C, Cr, Ni, Mo & N) are individually listed in the Table
5. All stainless steels contain Si, Mn, P & S. These are controlled to maximum % contents of typically 0.75% or 1.0%Si ~ 2.0%Mn ~ 0.015%S ~ 0.045%P.

   If these elements are intentionally added as alloying elements the higher % content is listed under "% Other"
6. The % content of any other alloying elements that are contained in some of the stainless steels is listed under "% Other"
7. Typical Proprietary Grades (which are commonly referred to in South Africa) are given for the purpose of example only. The inclusion of any such

   Proprietary Grade must not be interpreted as an endorsement or recommendation; and vice versa, the exclusion of any such Proprietary Grade must
   not be interpreted as a non-recommendation

ELECTRIC WELDED LOW CARBON STEEL PIPES FOR
AQUEOUS FLUIDS (ORDINARY DUTIES
(Metric Units)

1.     SCOPE

1.1 This specification covers Grade A, Grade B, and Grade C carbon steel pipes (of outside
          diameter 165-2 220 mm) for the conveyance of water and other aqueous fluids, and
          includes provision for pipes of steel that has superior physical properties to those of the steel
          specified for Grade C pipes

       NOTE
       a) The titles of standard referred to by number in the specification are given in

           Appendix A.
       b) Requirements that must be specified by the purchaser and those that must be agreed

           upon between purchaser and manufacturer are listed in Appendix B.
       c) Except under the standardization mark scheme, in the case of pipes required in exact

           lengths, arrangements for obtaining the sample(s) required in terms of 6.1 require special
           agreement between manufacturer and purchaser.

2.     DEFINITIONS

2.1 For the purposes of this specification the definitions given in SABS 044 and the following
          definitions shall apply:

       Acceptable. Acceptable to the purchaser but in relation to the standardization mark
       acceptable table to the South African Bureau of Standards.
       Defective. A pipe that fails in one or more respects to comply with the appropriate require-
       ments of the specification.
       Exact length. A length specified by the purchaser.
       Lot. Not more than the appropriate quantity given below, of pipes of the same grade and
       size, from one manufacturer, submitted at any one time for inspection and testing:

       Normal outside diameter, mm                 Quantity, max.
       Up to 620                                           200
       Above 620 up to and including 1 250                 100
       Above 1 250                                         50

       Pipe. A straight cylinder of uniform nominal inside diameter and having square-cut (plain
       or prepared) ends.
       Random length. A normal manufacturing length that is within a limited percentage (see
       4.1.1) of the average length required by the purchaser.

3.     MATERIAL

3.1 STEEL PLATE AND STRIP. The steel plates or strip used for the manufacture of the pipes shall
          have been produced by the electric furnace, basic open hearth, or basic
          oxygen process, and shall be free from seams, cracks, laminations, and other
          injurious defects.

3.2 CHEMICAL COMPOSITION. The ladle analysis of the steel shall, unless otherwise agreed
          upon between purchaser and manufacturer (see 3.3), comply with the requirements given in
          Table 1 appropriate to the grade of pipe specified by the purchaser.

TABLE 1 - CHEMICAL COMPOSITION AND PHYSICAL PROPERTIES OF STEELS

3.3 PHYSICAL PROPERTIES. The physical properties of the steel shall, unless the use of a steel
          having physical properties superior the those of Grade C has been agreed upon between
          purchaser and manufacturer, comply with the requirements given in Table 1 appropriate to
          the grade of pipe specified by the purchaser.

3.4 CERTIFICATION. When so required by the purchaser, the manufacturer shall make available
          to the purchser steel-maker' certificates covering all steel used in the manufacture of the
          pipes. These certificates shall include the process of manufacture, the chemical analysis,
          and the physical properties of the steel, except that, at the option of the pipe manufacturer,
          the physical properties of the steel may be determined on specimens taken from finished
          pipe.

4.     GENERAL REQUIREMENTS

4.1 DIMENSIONAL REQUIREMENTS

4.1.1  Length. The pipes shall be of random length or exact length, as required by the purchaser.
       Random lengths shall be between 4,5 m and 13,5 m. Not more than 10 per cent of random
       lengths shall be shorter than 75 per cent of the average length specified by the purchaser,
       and no pipe (other than a pipe from which a sample has been cut in terms of 6.1) shall be
       shorter than 40 per cent of this average length. Exact lengths shall be subject to tolerance of
       minus 0 mm or plus 15 mm.

4.1.2 OUTSIDE DIAMETER. The outside diameter of the pipe, determined in accordance with 7.1.1(a)
          or 7.1.1(b), as relevant, shall be as specified by the purchaser subject to the following toler-
          ances:

       a) Over the appropriate length (measured from each end of the pipe) given in Column 3 or
           5, as relevant, of Table 2: the corresponding tolerance given in Column 2 or 4.

       b) Over the rest of the pipe: the appropriate tolerance given in Table 3.

       Any out-of-roundness (other than that caused by sag), determined in accordance with
       7.1.1(b)(2), of pipes of nominal outside diameter (i.e. maximum ovality 2 per cent) or 6 mm,
       whichever is less.

TABLE 2 - TOLERANCES ON O.D. OF PIPE ENDS

4.1.3 WALL THICKNESS. The wall thickness shall be as agreed upon between the purchaser and
          the manufacturer, subject to a tolerance of plus 10 percent or minus 8 per cent.

4.1.4 STRAIGHTNESS. Any deviation of a pipe from straight, determined in accordance with 7.1.1,
          shall not exceed 0,2 per cent of the length of the pipe.

4.1.5 PIPE ENDS. Pipe ends shall be clean cut, free from burrs, and acceptably square to the axis
           of the pipe. They shall have been prepared for field welding or shall be plain, as specified
           by the purchaser.

       Ends prepared for field welding, shall, unless otherwise specified by the purchaser, be
       prepared in accordance with Figure 1, and the root face shall not deviate from squareness
       to the axis of the pipe by more than the appropriate of the following:

       a) Pipes of outside diameter not exceeding 500 mm: 1,5 mm
       b) Larger pipes: 3 mm

4.2 FABRICATION

4.2.1  FORMING. Pipes shall have been fabricated from plates or strip formed, rolled, or pressed to
       a cylindrical form and joined by one or more longitudinal seams (with or without circumfer-
       ential seams), or from strip formed or rolled to a cylindrical form and joined by a helical
       seam. Circumferential joints shall be at least 1,5 m apart, and the longitudinal welds of
       mated sections shall be at least 30░ apart.

4.2.2 WELDS

4.2.2.1 GENERAL. All welds shall be acceptable electric fusion or electric resistance welds and shall
           comply with the requirements given in 4.2.2.2 or 4.2.2.3, as relevant.

4.2.2.2 ELECTRIC FUSION WELDS

       a) Shape of profile. The profile of a weld shall be slightly convex or shall be flush with the
           wall of the pipe, and it shall merge smoothly into the parent metal.

       b) Uniformity of appearance. The face of a weld shall be substantially uniform in
           appearance throughout its length.

       c) Overlap. There shall be no overlap at the toes of a weld.
       d) Undercut. Welds be substantially free from undercut and if present

       1) the depth of the undercut shall not exceed 12,5 per cent of the nominal wall thickness
           or 1 mm, whichever is less, and

       2) the aggregate length of undercut in any 1 m length of weld shall not exceed 50 mm.

       e) Penetration bead. In butt welds made from one side only, a slight penetration bead
           should be present, but absence of a penetration bead shall be permitted in isolated
           places provided that there is complete root fusion.

       f) Root groove. In butt welds made from one side only, a root groove may be present
           provided that it has a rounded outline and does not penetrate below the level of the
           adjacent surfaces of the parent plate.

       g) Weld reinforcements. The heights of outer and inner weld reinforcements shall not exceed
           3 mm in pipes of wall thickness not exceeding 10 mm, and 5 mm in pipes having thicker
           walls, except that when so required by the purchaser the height of the inner weld
           reinforcement shall not exceed 1 mm

       h) Freedom from cracks. The weld metal, the heat-affected zone, and the surrounding
           parent metal shall be free from cracks.

       i) Freedom from surface defects. The weld face shall be free from porosity, cavities, and
           trapped slag.

       j) Transverse tensile strength of welded joints. Test specimens, prepared and tested in
           accordance with 7.2.1, shall have an ultimate tensile strength equal to at least 95 per
           cent of the minimum specified for the appropriate parent plate (see Table 1).

       k) Resistance to bending. Test specimens, prepared and tested in accordance with 7.2.2
           shall, except at the arrises, show no crack (on the outer surface) of length or width
           greater than 3 mm.

4.2.2.3 ELECTRIC RESISTANCE WELDS

       a) Uniformity of appearance. A weld shall be substantially uniform in appearence and
           shall show full fusion throughout its length.

       b) Upset metal and flash. The height of upset metal and flash on the outer surface shall not
           exceed 1mm and, when so required by the purchaser, this requirement shall also apply
           to the inner surface. Any surface indentations resultant from the removal of excess
           material shall be such that

                                   22
SABS 719 - 1971                                                                               MINING
                                                                                            PRESSURE
                                                                                             SYSTEMS

                                                                                            Deep down, we care

4.2.3  1) their depth does not exceed 12.5 per cent of the nominal wall thickness or 1 mm,
4.2.4      whichever is less, and

       2) their aggregate length in any 1 m length of weld does not exceed 50 mm.

       c) Freedom from cracks. The joint, the heat-affected zone, and the parent metal shall be
           free from cracks.

       d) Transverse tensile strength of welded joint. Test specimens prepared and tested in
           accordance with 7.2.1, shall have an ultimate tensile strength equal to at least 95 per
           cent of the minimum specified for the appropriate parent plate (see Table 1).

       e) Resistance to flattening. Test specimens, prepared and tested in accordance with 7.2.3,
           shall show no cracks on the outer surface.

       RECTIFICATION OF DEFECTS. Welded seams and surface defects (i.e. defects which would
       not have caused leaks) in the parent metal that have been repaired by welding shall be
       permitted, provided that the welds comply with the requirements of 4.2.2.2 or 4.2.2.3, as
       relevant.

       RESISTANCE TO HYDRAULIC PRESSURE. When tested in accordance with 7.3, pipes shall be
       capable of withstanding without leaking or bursting, the hydraulic test pressure calculated
       from the following formula 1, subject , unless otherwise agreed upon between the purchaser
       and the manufacturer, to a maximum of 70 bar:

       P=15  xY  x  t
              D

       where     P = hydraulic test pressure
                 Y = minimum specified yield stress of steel plate or strip, MPa (see 3.3)

                 t = nomimal wall thickness of pipe, mm

                 D = nomimal outside diameter of pipe, mm

4.2.5  COATINGS AND LININGS. When so required by the purchaser, the pipes shall have been
5.     cleaned and coated or lined (or both) in accordance with the relevant requirements of
5.1    SABS 720, or as agreed upon between the purchaser and the manufacturer.
6.
6.1    MARKING

6.2    The name or the trade name or the trade mark of the manufacturer and any other markings
       required by the purchaser shall be legibly painted or stencilled on each pipe.

       SAMPLING AND COMPLIANCE WITH THE SPECIFICATION2)

       SAMPLING. After each pipe has been inspected and tested as described in 7.1 and 7.3, the
       following sampling procedure shall be applied in determining whether a lot complies with
       the appropriate requirements of the specification, except that, by agreement between the
       purchaser and the manufacturer, this procedure may be waived in the case of submerged-
       arc welded pipes provided that the manufacturer is able to satisfy the purchaser that the
       welding procedure and the production control is such as to ensure that all welds will
       comply with the requirements of 4.2.2.2(j) and (k).

       a) First sample. From an end of one pipe taken at random from the lot cut a section long
           enough to provide the appropriate test specimens required in terms of 7.2.

       b) Second sample. If a test specimen from the first sample fails to comply with the
           appropriate requirements, cut a section (long enough to provide the specimen for each
           test that the first sample failed) from each of 2 further pipes taken at random from the lot.

       c) Third sample. If a test specimen from the second sample fails to comply with the
           appropriate requirements, cut a similar section from each pipe in the lot or each of 10

       further pipes taken a random from the lot, whichever is less.

       NOTE: When pipes of exact length are required, the samples shall be taken before the pipe
       is cut to exact length.

       COMPLIANCE. The lot shall be deemed to comply with the requirements of the specification
       if

       a) after inspection and testing of the lot in terms of 7.1 and 7.3 no defective is found, and
       b) after testing of the first sample no defective is found, or
       c) after testing of the second sample no defective is found, or
       d) after testing of the third sample no defective is found.

7.     INSPECTION AND METHODS OF TEST
7.1
7.1.1  INSPECTION

7.1.2  DIMENSIONS Using, unless otherwise specified, any methods that will provide the required
7.2    accuracy, measure the dimensions of each pipe in the lot for compliance with 4.1. In the
7.2.2  cases of measurements of outside diameter and out-of-roundness follow the following rules:
7.2.3
7.3    a) Pipes of nominal outside diameter not exceeding 500 mm. Use ring gauges to check the ends
7.4        of the pipes, and use any acceptable method to check the body.

       b) Pipes of nominal outside diameter greater than 500 mm.

       1) Outside diameter. Use a diameter tape to check the outside diameter of both the pipe
           ends and the body.

       2) Out-of-roundness. Use any acceptable method to determine the actual maximum and
           minimum values of the outside diameter (i.e. the measured values corrected, when
           relevant, for sag). Check that neither of these values varies from the nominal diameter by
            more than 1 per cent or 6 mm, as relevant.

       WELDS. After inspecting each pipe in the lot for compliance with 4.2.1, visually examime all
       the welds, the heat-affected zones, and the surrounding parent metal in each pipe for com-
       pliance with the requirements of 4.2.2.2 or 4.2.2.3 (as appropriate) and, when relevant, 4.2.3.

       TRANSVERSE TENSILE TEST. From a cold-flattened secton of pipe cut a test specimen con-
       forming to Figure 2. Do not remove the weld reinforcement. Determine the ultimate tensil
       strength (UTS) by the method given in SABS 054.

       ROOT BEND TEST (Electric Fusion Welds). From a cold-flattened or as-cut section of pipe,
       cut a specimen conforming to Figure 3. Remove the weld reinforcement and file the arrises
       to a radius not exceeding 10 per cent of the thickness of the specimen. Bend through an
       angle of at least 180░ in a rig conforming to Figure 3. Check for compliance with the
       requirements of 4.2.2.2(k).

       FLATTENING TEST (Electric Resistance Welds). Cut a cylindrical test specimen conforming
       to Figure 4. Ensuring that the weld is at the point of maximum bending (see Figure 4), flatten
       the specimen between two parallel flat surfaces until the outside diameter to which the
       compression is applied is reduced to not more than two-thirds of its original value.

       HYDRAULIC TEST. Subject each pipe in the lot to the relevant hydraulic test pressure speci-
       fied in 4.2.4 and (while it is under pressure) hammer-test each end of the pipe in an accept-
       able manner. Maintain the pressure for the length of time necessary to inspect the welds for
       leaks and to check for compliance with the requirements of 4.2.4.

       COATINGS AND LININGS. When applicable, inspect and test the coatings and linings of the
       pipes, using the relevant methods given in SABS 720.

       1) The hydraulic test pressure calculated from the formula will be such as to subject the
           pipe to 75 per cent of the specified ninimum yield stress of the steel plate or strip.

       2) This section applies to the sampling for inspection and testing before acceptance or
           rejection of single lots (consignments) in cases where no information about the
           implementation of quality control or testing during manufacture is available to help in
           assessing the quality of the lot. It is also used as the procedure for adjudicating in cases
           of dispute.

SUPERHYDROLOCK

A uniform pipe connector for test
pressures up to 1000 bar. The pres-
sure actuated radial seals will not
leak, even if the hubs move slightly
apart.

SEGLOCK PIPE CONNECTOR

The perfectly designed high pres-

 NB250 and bigger. The segments
  achieve full seating on the hubs
 which large 2-clamp connectors

LINER INTEGRITY SECURED

Conventional methods require the stressing of
the liner in order to insert it into the host pipe
(usually by taking a slightly oversize liner and
stretching it axially to make it fit the host). When
the axial pressure is released, the liner returns to
its normal diameter, thus ensuring a tight fit to the
host. Whilst this is technically satisfactory, it leaves
the liner tube weakened, especially at the
flanges, which then fail in operation. The new MPS
system overcomes this completely, because
when the water pressure is released in the
annular space, the liner (HDPE pipe), immediately returns to its normal diameter, sealing to
the inside of the host (steel pipe), without having to stretch the liner in any way. There is
therefore no weakening of the liner material or liner flanges.

FLOW MAXIMISED

The MPS `HDPE Tight Lining' System not only ensures liner integrity, but maximum flow as
well. Although the cross sectional area of the flow is reduced once the MPS liner is inserted,
this is minimised by the tight fit and more than compensated for by the very smooth walls
of the HDPE liner which accelerate flow. These improved flow characteristics will typically
remain intact for the lifespan of the piping system

WHY HDPE ?

BY definition HPDE has the ability to withstand shock loading as well as torsional stressing.
HDPE's thermal conductivity makes it capable of being repeatedly softened and hard-
ened through application of heat or cooling.

Like all plastics (organic polymers), HDPE is a chemical compound of carbon combined
with elements such as hydrogen, chlorine, oxgen or nitrogen. High Density Polyethylenes
have the additional characteristics of high impact strength and high resistance to corro-
sion, both internally and externally in the case of piping. This makes HDPE an ideal pipe
liner.

UNIQUE FLARING PROCESS

Once the HDPE liner is inserted into the steel
pipes, the liner ends are flared up onto the steel
pipe flanges to create a perfect sealing surface.
This means that once the line is bolted up, no
gasket is necessary at the correct torque ratio.

Flaring of the HDPE liner ends is very carefully
controlled. No butting, fusion or electrostatic
welding is used in creating flares. Instead, the
protruding HDPE liner ends are heated carefully
with hot air blowers to the correct melt point
temperature for HDPE. At this point the HDPE is
flared onto the steel flanges. Each flare is right up to the bolt holes of the flange.

Each flare surface features a `gramophone' finish for better sealing and there is no radius
or broken corners on the inside diameter of the flares; only a sharp corner which gives a
bigger seaing surface.

137
HIGH DENSITY POLYETHYLENE LINERS                                 MINING
                                                               PRESSURE
                                                                SYSTEMS

                                                               Deep down, we care

ON SITE RE-LINING

MPS Liners also offers a unique re-lining service
for existing pipe lines. The pipeline is shut down
and dissembled. Each individual pipe is then
cleaned and cleared of all clusterisation
using a special pull-through instrument, before
being re-lined with the HPDE inners and properly
flared. The pipes are then re-bolted and the
pipeline re-commissioned.

FACTORY RE-LINING

The recommended procedure is for MPS to
dismantle the pipeline and transport the
individual pipes to its factory in Boksburg. Here the pipes are properly cleaned and de-
clusterised (and replaced if damaged or corroded). This ensures the highest quality,
saving of renewal costs and longevity of the customer's pipeline.

tance of this parameter in the design of
the system.

Most plastic pipes normally have a very
smooth surface and consequently have a
lower pressure drop over a certain dis-
tance. This can result in higher volume,
increased velocity or decreased pumping
costs or a combination of those.

The Flow Nomogram gives an easy way to
determine the pressure loss in a pipeline at

HAZEN WILLIANS CO-EFFICIENT FOR DIFFERENT PIPE MATERIALS

One method of expressing the roughness and flow in a pipeline is the Hazen Williams
equation, ie.

V = 0,849 C x R0.63 x S0.54

where
C is the "Hazen Williams" co-efficient
V is velocity of flow
R is the hydraulic radius
S is the head (or pressure) loss

Below are the values for C for different pipe materials.

LIFE

Although the design standard is 50 years, it might be necessary in some cases to design
for a shorter expected life of the pipeline. This is done only for economical reasons and it
should be remembered that it disqualifies the pipe for a SABS mark of approval.

Factors other than pressure and temperature also have an influence on the expected life
of the pipeline, such as abrasion or chemical reaction by the fluid being transported.

Abrasion resistance of HDPE and PP is excellent as can be seen from the curves in Graph
7. HDPE in particular, is increasingly being used in high abrasion applications, such as coal
washing plants and slurry lines.

CHEMICAL RESISTANCE

Both HDPE and PP have excellent resistance to most chemicals under ambient
temperature conditions.

RESISTANCE FACTORS FOR HDPE

The information contained in the table is intended as
a preliminary guide to the chemical resistance of
HDPE; it does not provide sufficient information for
evaluating the use of HDPE for specific applications or
operating conditions. Thus effluent pipes, for example,
have satisfactory resistance to all the wastes normally
occurring in the chemical industry.

To obtain a better assessment of the ressistance of
pressure pipes to particular media, it is necessary to
carry out creep rupture tests under internal pressure
on pipe specimens. Instead of water, the pipe is filled
with the chemicals to be tested such as acids, alkalis
or solvents.

The service life measured in this way is compared
with that for pipes tested with water. The time quotient
fcrt (= service life with the test medium/service life with water) is a measure of the chemi-
cal resistance of the pipe under stress.

Instead of the time factor, the decrease (or increase) of the stress for the same service life
can be used.

RESISTANCE TO CHEMICALS AND OTHER MEDIA

Because of their non-polar nature as high-molecular paraffinic hydrocarbons, «Hostalen,
«Hostalen PP and «Hostalen LD, the polyolefins of Hoechst, have exceptionally high resis-
tance to chemicals and other media. They are not attacked by aqueous solutions of salts,
acids and alkalis. Fats, oils and waxes cause only slight swelling.

Up to 60░C, Hostalen, Hostalen PP and Hostalen LD are resistant to many solvents; at higher
temperatures they are attacked by aromatic and halogenated hydrocarbons.

Hostalen, Hostalen PP and Hostalen LD are not resistant to strong oxidizing agents such as
nitric acid, oleum and halogens.

Generally speaking, higher temperatures can considerably impair resistance, depending
on the chemical environment.

Owing to its lower density and higher degree of branching, Hostalen LD is not quite as
resistant as Hostalen. But the difference is merely one of degree; its EVA copolymers con-
taining a large proportion of vinyl acetate have much poorer resistance.

The results of numerous chemical resistance tests are shown in the following table. They
summarise the changes that were observed when Hostalen, Hostalen PP and Hostalen LD
were exposed to the substances listed. They cannot, however, replace chemical resistance
tests which are conducted as part of studies to determine general suitability of design; nor
do these results hold for all application situations.

A special assessment must always be made if the substrate is exposed to mechanical,
chemical and possibly also thermal stresses at the time, as is the case with pressure pipes
or large tanks. The so-called resistance factor (fcr)* is a valuable guide in such cases. It
characterises the long-term resistance of pipes exposed to a certain substance relative to
the long-term resistance in water. In the case of pipes made from Hostalen and Hostalen
PP resistance factors were determined for a number of substances.

Plastics specimens were placed in the relevant substance for 60 days (30 days in the case
of LDPE) but were not subjected to mechanical stress. They were then tested for swelling or
weight loss and subjected to the test for tensile strength.

Specimens: 50 mm x 25 mm x 1 mm and specimen 3 according to DIN 43455, with dimen-
tions in the ratio 1 : 4, both taken from press-moulded sheets.

1. GENERAL                                                                  SYSTEMS

                                                                           Deep down, we care

Rubbers are elastomeric polymers consisting of long chain macromolecules.

On mixing with suitable reactants that form strong chemical bonds, the rubber changes
from a deformable substance into an elastic material.

In principle the nature of the elastomer determines the basic properties of the products manu-
factured from it. However, these properties may be significantly modified by the use of other
compounding ingredients. The physical and chemical properties of linings can be designed
over a wide field of applications by the selection of a suitable type of polymer, amount and
type of filler, process aids and other additives as well as the vulcanization system used.

The use of fillers Г aside from the vulcanization system used Г is of utmost impotance in order
to obtain the desired properties of a lining. Fillers should therefore be looked upon as quality
enhancing materials, rather than cost cutting ones. The application of inactive fillers such as
re-ground rubber (crumb) should be avoided as it could affect properties such as curing,
abrasion resistance and adhesion to rigid substrates.

The rubbers resulting from selective compounding with varying proportions of sulphur may
be classified in two groups: soft and hard (ebonite).

SOFT RUBBERS

Soft rubber linings normally have a hardness range 40 - 80 shore A and are obtained by
using small amounts of vulcanizing agent which gives a low proportion of cross links. Soft
rubbers may be sesigned to have good chemical resistance, high resilience and excellent
abrasion resistance and are often used for lining ball mill, coal hoppers and pipes for
conveying sand.

The temperature range for continuouse use could be between -30░C and 90░C.

HARD RUBBERS

Certain rubbers can be converted into hard rubber or ebonite by saturation with higher
levels of sulphur.

Ebonites can be produced from natural lor synthetic isoprenes, styrene Г butadiene,
acrylonitrile butadiene and polybutadiene of blends of them. Ebonites have a hardness
range 25 Г 80 shore D and are characterized by high tensile strength and low elongation
@ break. Hard rubbers generally have higher chemical resistance than soft rubbers based
on the same polymer types, especially to chlorine gas and most aliphatic carboxylic acids
and are used where maximum resistance to leaching is required. They are normally used
within the temperature range 0░C - 100░C. For lower operating tyemperatures ebonites may
be modified with flexibilizers.

2. SELECTION OF LINING

          Because the properties of rubber linings vary widely, the selection of the type of material to
          be used for a specific application must be done in consultation with the lining contractor.

2.1 PHYSICAL & CHEMICAL PROPERTIES OF LINING

          Rubber based materials can be chemically or physically degraded by the action of liquids
          or gases with which they come into contact.

          The rate and extent of the attack depends on the chemical composition of the rubber
          polymer and other compounding ingredients as well as the nature of the liquid of gas, its
          concentration, temperature, pressure and duration of contact.

          In broad terms, harder rubbers are preferred for high chemical resistance and for
          combating high impact / cutting forces that often occur when handling coarse materials.
          Low durometer rubbers (gum stocks i.e. 96 % NR) give excellent results when used in
          abrasive slurry service or sliding abrasion where fine to medium size particles are being
          handled. However, other physical properties often play a significant role in optimizing
          performance. For example, good resilience is required when handling or screening sticky
          materials and elongation is an important factor in the design of fabricated seals & bellows.
          Different rubber compounds exhibit varying degrees of resistance to chemicals.

155
POLYMER LINING SYSTEMS    MINING
                        PRESSURE
                         SYSTEMS

                        Deep down, we care

ISO / TR 7620 Г 1986 (E) provides a guide to the suitability of various elastomers for service in
different fluids and chemicals.

The properties of various polymers are summarized as follows, but are intended as a guide
only. For more precise information, advice should be sought from the rubber manufacturer.

NATURAL RUBBER (NR) OR SYNTHETIC POLYIOSPRENE (R)

(SABS 1198 - 1978: Type 1)

Vulcanized compounds based on polyisoprene rubber are resistant to most inorganic
chemicals, with the exception of strong oxidizing agents such as chromic and nitric acid,
unless these are present in very small proportions. They are resistant to a wide range of
organic chemicals, including alcohols and other oxygen derivatives. They should not be
used with aliphatic, aromatic and halogenated hydrocarbons, mineral oils, vegetable oils
and some esters.

Basic selection guide for NR (Type 1):

и Gum Stock:- This is the premium selection in soft rubber for superior resistance to wet
  abrasion (must contain a minimum of 90% NR by volume).

и Soft Rubber:- A cheaper alternative where the softness is specified over and above the
  physical properties.

и Hard Rubber:- (70 Г 80 shore A):- Preferred for high chemical resistance and for handling
  coarse materials.

и Ebonite (60 Г 80 shore D):- High chemical resistance but not suitable for cutting abrasion
  from coarse particles.

When suitably compounded, polyisoprene can be used in the temperature range -30░C to
+100░C (soft rubber) and 5░C to 100░C (ebonite).

STYRENE Г BUTADIENE RUBBER (SBR)

(SABS 1198 - 1978: Type 1)

Co-polymers of styrene butadiene have properties broadly similar to those of polyisoprene
rubbers, when compounded for the same duties

BUTYL RUBBER (IIR)

(SABS 1198 - 1978: Type 2)

Butyl rubber is a co-polymer of isobutylene with small proportions of isoprene. Butyl rubbers
cannot be compounded to form ebonite.

Due to its limited degree of chemical unsaturation it possesses greater chemical and heat
resistance than natural rubber / polyisoprene, especially to oxidizing agents. Butyl rubbers
have low gas permeability and when suitably compounded, lower water absorption than
most other rubbers.

Butyl rubber is resistant to polar solvents, such as methanol, ethanol and acetone, and also
to low molecular weight carboxylic acids and esters and to most oils of vegetable and
animal origin. Resistance to aqueous solutions is generally very good. Strong acids (HCI)
and alkalis (NaOH) do not attack butyl rubber. Degradation takes place in concentrated
oxidizing acids (H2SO4 / HNO3), but not in dilute solutions.

Butyl rubber vulcanizates should not be used in the presence of free halogens, mineral oils
and halogenated or aromatic hydrocarbons.

Halogenated (chlorinated / brominated) butyl rubbers, which are easier to process, are
also available. The low degree of unsaturation in butyl rubbers gives very low rates of cure
with vulcanization systems used successfully for NR or SBR. Halogenation of butyl rubber
causes an increase in reactivity during vulcanization and improves the compatibility of butyl
with general purpose rubbers. It does not affect the low gas permeability or heat chemical
resistance.

The aspects, which affect the selecion of halogenated butyl rubbers are connected
primarily to vulcanization. Chlorobutyl is more active in crosslinking than regular than
regular butyl, bromobutyl, in turn, is more active than chlorobutyl. Longer cure times can be
expected when using CIIR, and the level of valcanizing agents may have to be adjusted in
order to optimize vulcanizate properties.

Butyl rubber can be used with in the temperature range -30░C to +120░C.

156
POLYMER LINING SYSTEMS              MINING
                                  PRESSURE
                                   SYSTEMS

                                  Deep down, we care

NITRILE RUBBER (NBR & XNBR)

(SABS 1198 - 1978: Type 3)

Acrylonitrile butadiene co-polymer (NBR) and its variant, carboxylated nitrile rubber (XNBR),
have excellent resistance to swelling by mineral oils & fuels.

The concentration of the acrylonitrile in the copolymer has a considerable influence on the
swelling resistance of the vulcanizates in non-polar solvents. High acrylonitrile to butadiene
ratios will give the best resistance and also have lower gas permeability. Higher butadiene
ratios give better elastic and low temperature properties. Carboxylated NBR is used in
combination with butadiene rubbers for outstanding abrasion resistance.

The polymers should not be used with phenols, ketones, strong acetic acids, aromatic
hydrocarbons or nitrogen derivatives. Nitrile rubber linings with similar physical properties to
polyisoprene can be prepared suitable for use within the temperature range -20░C to +110░C
(soft rubber) and 20░C to 115░C (ebonite).

CHLOROPRENE RUBBER (CR)

(SABS 1198 - 1978: Type 4)

Polychloroprene gives lining compounds with greater resistance to heat, ozone, and sunlight
and also has medium resistance to oil. It has the property of inhibiting the growth of marine
and certain other organisms.

Polychloroprene should not be used with halogenated or aromatic hydrocarbons.

Selected polymer grades can be used continuously within the temperature range -20░C to
+110░C depending on the polymer crystallinity and compound design. Chloroprene cannot
be compounded to form ebonite.

CHLOROSULPHONATED POLYETHYLENE (CSM)

(SABS 1198 - 1978: Type 5)

Chlorosulphonated polyethylene (Hypalon) is a synthetic polymer with excellent resistance
to heat, abrasion, ozone and oxidizing chemicals such a sodium hypochlorite. It can be
compounded to handle up to 95% sulphuric acid and is often used for reaction vessels
where temperature and concentration of acids fluctuate to a wide degree.

CSM has good resistance to most oils, lubricants and aliphatic hydrocarbons, but is
unsuitable for use in contact with esters and ketones. The range of temperatures in which it
can be used continuously is -5░C to +120░C.

ETHYLENE PROPYLENE RUBBERS (EPM OR EPDM)

(Not classified by SABS 1198 - 1978)

Ethylene propylene rubbers are available as EPM (copolymer from ethylene and propylene)
and as EPDM (terpolymer based on ethylene, propylene and a non-conjugated diene). The
molecules of these rubbers have completely saturated hydrocarbon main chains, through
which excellent ozone resistance and very good resistance to heat and oxidation is
obtained.

Lining materials based on these polymers have very good resistance to acids, alkalis, salts,
ozone and many organic chemicals but cannot be used with oils, hydrocarbons and
chlorinated solvents.

EPDM has no polar groups and is therefore difficult to bond to metal or othe substrtated. As
the oil content has an adverse effect on bonding, it is advisable to use a medium molecular
weight EPDM grade, which requires less oil. Better results are also obtained with grades with
a high degree of unsaturation.

Polymers may be compounded for use within the temp range -30░C to +110░C for peroxide
cured compounds.

BUTADIENE RUBBER (BR)

(SABS 1198 - 1978: Type 1)

Butaiene rubber is normally used in combination with polyisoprene or carboxylated nitrile
rubber to produce linings with superior abrasion resistance compared to the individual
rubbers and to inmprove the lower temperature properties of the rubber.

                             157
POLYMER LINING SYSTEMS                                      MINING
                                                          PRESSURE
                                                           SYSTEMS

                                                          Deep down, we care

COPOLYMERS OF HEXAFLUOROPROPYLENE AND VINYLIDENEFLUORIDE

(Not classified by SABS 1198 - 1978)

Copolymers of hexafluoropropylene and vinylidenefluoride (Viton) are synthetic rubbers
with outstanding heat and fluid resistance and are of considerable interest as protective
lining materials for tanks and other equipment in chemical and solvent service.

Except for the use of Litharge rather than Magnesia when acid resistance is required, the
compounding ingredients normally used with Viton have relatively little effect on fluid
resistance.

These materials have excellent resistance to oils, fuels, lubricants, carbon tetrachloride, most
concentrated acids and to many aliphatic and aromatic hydrocarbons such as toluene,
benzene and xylene. They can be used in contact with many corrosive gases, e.g. bromine
and chlorine, but they are attacked by ammonia. They should not be used in contact with
low molecular weight esters and ethers, ketones, certain amines or hot anhydrous
hydrofluoric and chlorosulphonic acids.

Viton vulcanizates have exellent weather resistance and do not crack in ozone. Standard
Viton compounds do not have good resistance to high-pressure steam, but fair resistance to
steam can be obtained by suitable compounding.

2.2 SERVICE CONDITIONS

          The selection of an appropriate rubber will depend on the properties of the rubber as well
          as on a number of optional, physical and environmental factors, which must be clearly
          specified before a material can be selected:

          и Ingredients
          и Design of Equipment
          и Temperature
          и Angle of Impact & Sliding Wear
          и Velocity of Particles
          и Particle Size and Weight
          и Noise & Vibration
          и Degree of Vacuum or Pressure
          и Cycle of Operations
          и Mechanical Damage
          и Special Requirements
          и Costs

2.2.1 INGREDIENTS

          и Chemical concentrations of all ingredients, including defoamers, additives & impurities in
          the solution to be handled.

          Where concentrations are low. from 0 Г 5 %, it is often preferable to use hard or semi-hard
          rubber linings, especially at higher temperatures (65░C Г 85░C), because of their superior
          water resistance when compared with soft rubber. It is important to list all these ingredients,
          as certain materials may not remain totally in solution. They may concentrate on the
          bottom, on the top (liquid vapor phase), or volatilize in the vapor phase above the liquid
          level.

2.2.2 DESIGN OF EQUIPMENT

          и Size, shape and dimensions of tank and equipment, including drawings if possible.
          и Dimensions, wall thickness & type of flanges or couplings for pipe systems.

          Pipes and tanks must be fabricated and welded in accordance with specified codes. Welds
          must have a round and smooth surface suitable for applying rubber lining and must be
          certified free of defects before lining commences (i.e. dye penetrant inspection).

                                      158
POLYMER LINING SYSTEMS                                             MINING
                                                                 PRESSURE
                                                                  SYSTEMS

                                                                 Deep down, we care

2.2.3 TEMPERATURE

и Minimum, Maximum & Normal Operating Temperatures
и Cycle of Temperature

At elevated temperatures, the chemical effect on the lining is accelerated and the effects of
oxidation and diffusion are more rapid, so that the overall life of the lining will be shorter
than it would at room temperature.

2.2.4 ANGLE OF IMPACT & SLIDING WEAR

          The angle of impact of the particle relative to the wear surface is important in the design of
          rubber linings.

          At an impact angle of 90░, resilience is the major factor resisting wear. As the impact angle
          reduces to around 50░, tear resistance becomes more important. At very low impact angles
          slurries are the best handled by flat sheet. This also applies to pulley lagging and other
          applications involving general sliding wear.

Figure 1 demonstrates the effect of impact angles on wear rate.

                 EFFECT OF IMPACT ANGLE ON WEAR RATE

ANGLE OF IMPACT  100
                  90
                  80     10 20 30 40 50 60 70 80 90
                  70
                  60
                  50
                  40
                  30
                  20
                  10
                    0
                      0

                         PERCENT INCREASE IN WEAR RATE

2.2.5 VOLOCITY OF PARTICLES

          In the case of impact and sliding abrasion there is a critical speed above which
          elastomers are unable to recover and absorb energy. In this case the product's resilience
          cannot be used to its full extent and the surface may deteriorate more rapidly. This normally
          applies to velocities above 10m/s.

2.2.6 PARTICLE SIZE, WEIGHT & SHAPE

          In order to achieve the best possible operating economy and the longest service life it is
          usual to increase rubber thickness within certain limits to cope with larger and heavier
          particles. Impact of particles from increasing height also requires increased rubber thickness
          to absorb the compressive forces.

          As the particle hits the surface, the rubber deforms, absorbing the kinetic energy of the
          particle. The resilient nature of rubber returns most of this energy to the particle causing it to
          rebound. There will be little or no wear and no permanent deformation.

                         159
POLYMER LINING SYSTEMS                                                       MINING
                                                                           PRESSURE
                                                                            SYSTEMS

                                                                           Deep down, we care

However, if the particle momentum is too great relative to the rubber thickness, the impact
force cannot be absorbed and the rubber may break down due to fatigue.

Table 1 provides a guide for thickness selection based on handling crushed stone.

          Consider any difficulties expected in the handling and final siting of the equipment as well
          as any vibration of the equipment and the possibility of mechanical damage.

          и Metal fabrication
          и Protection of the tank
          и Transport
          и Storage
          Special requirements specified by engineering company or end user, must be agreed upon
          by all parties concerned prior to fabrication. Consider extremes of weather likely to be
          encountered during the installation, handling, transport and storage of equipment, etc.

3. DESIGNATION OF LININGS             SYSTEMS

          (As per SABS 1198 - 1978)  Deep down, we care

SABS 1198: 1978 classifies linings in accordance with the type of basic polymer, the grade
(based on a minimum value of the tensile strength), and the class (based on the hardness).
Provision is made for specifying certain additional special properties.

3.1 LINE CALL-OUT

          The properties required of a lining by a purchaser shall be specified by a line call-out that
          comprises the following:

          a) The appropriate type number given in Table 2; followed by
          b) The appropriate grade letter given in 4.2; followed by
          c) The appropriate class number given in 4.3; followed, when relevant, by
          d) The Roman numerals in the series I to VII appropriate to the special properties
          (see 4.4) required.

        EXAMPLE: The line call Г out 4B 60(II) (IV) represents a lining based on a chloroprene

          polymer that has a minimum tensile strength of 14 Mpa and a nominal hardness of 60 shore
          A or IRH degrees, and that must be resistant to ozone and to abrasion.

        NOTE: The full combination of the special properties required by a purchaser may not

          always be available (see Tables 3 Г 7), and under these circumstances a compromise might
          have to be reached. If special properties other than those listed in 4.4 are required, the
          purchaser and the lining contractor must agree on the values and methods of test for these
          properties.

3.2 AMPLIFICATION OF A LINE CALL-OUT

          The line call-out shall (when and as relevant) be amplified in respect of the special proper-
          ties as follows:

          a) When heat resistance (I) is required, the purchaser shall specify whether the lining is to be
              rated as resistant up to 80░C or up to 100░C and whether the temperature will be applied
              continuously or intermittently.

          b) When resistance to chemicals (III) is required, the purchaser shall specify the chemical
              and the maximum operating temperature.

          c) When resistance to abrasion (IV) is required, the values and the methods of tests shall be
              agreed upon between the purchaser and the contractor.

          d) When resistance to release of contaminants (V) is required, the purchaser shall specify
              the chemical.

4. REQUIREMENTS FOR LININGS

          (SABS 1198 - 1978 - amended)

          When the applicator is responsible for selecting the grade of lining to be applied, he shall
          verify that such lining will withstand the chemical and physical conditions specified.

          When the purchaser selects the grade of lining to be applied, the applicator shall be
          responsible only for the correct application.

          A lining shall be of one of the appropriate (see Tables 3 Г 7) of the following grades, as

4.3 CLASS

A lining (other than a Type 1, Grade D lining) shall be of one of the following classes, as
specified by the purchaser: 40, 50, 60, or 70.

When tested under laboratory conditions, hardness reading shall conform to the specified
hardness (shore A or IRHD) to within +/- 5░.

4.4 SPECIAL PROPERTIES

          When so required by the purchaser (see 3.21), a lining shall have one or more of the
          applicable (see Table 3 - 7) of the following special properties:

          I: Resistance to heat (rated for use at a temperature of up to 80░C or up to 100░C
                 (See 3.2 (a))

          II: Resistance to ozone
          III: Resistance to chemicals (i.e. to a specific chemical up to a specific maximum

                 operating temperature (see 3.2 (b))
          IV: Abrasion resistance (see 3.2 (c))
          V: Resistance to release of contaminants (by a specific chemical (see 3.2 (d))
          VI: Resistance to water
          VII: Resistance to oil (type of oil must be specified)

          Unless previous experience demonstrates that a lining will be suitable for a particular duty,
          appropriate testing shall be carried out.

4.5 THICKNESS OR RUBBER SHEETING

          The thickness of the lining shall be selected to suit the chemical and or mechanical duty as
          specified by the purchaser. It shall be at least 3.0mm thick and preferably one of the
          thickness requirements in column 1 of table 8.

          Sheets shall be prepared from at least two plies by calendering and sheets of one of the
          preferred nominal thicknesses shall consist of at least the appropriate minimum number of
          plies given in column 2 of table 8. The number of plies in sheets of other thickness
          requirements shall be as specified by the purchaser.

          The actual thickness of a sheet, determined in accordance with 9.13 shall not differ from the
          nominal value by more than 5 %

          Table 8 Г Number of Plies

                1               2

4.6 VISUAL INSPECTION OF UNVULCANIZED RUBBER SHEETING

          Before proceeding with the lining operation, the applicator shall ensure that all materials to
          be used are visually examined to ensure that they have no imperfection, which could
          significantly affect the performance of the finished vulcanized lining.

          Inspection for visible defects shall be carried out over the entire surface of the lining in good
          light, attention being paid to any areas of mechanical damage, cuts, blisters, lack of
          adhesion & poor jointing.

          If the applicator finds a defect prior to vulcanization it shall be removed and the area
          overlaid with unvulcanized rubber of the same type as the original unvulcanized rubber.
